<div id="review_2277009502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277009502" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2277009502?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405291460" href="/book/show/39067298-the-poet-x">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277009502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4153704078689494257">I knew I'd love this one!! I just needed !! to hurry up !! and read it. (Wow I am just so behind on so many releases.) This was so heartfelt and emotional, I just truly felt my soul flooded with feelings, hopeful ones and hurt ones. It's the kind of book that can brilliantly draw you in and paint you a whole world of feelings with just a few lines. The author is a master with words and these skills...I just. It's such a good book.<br/><br/>I didn't realise this was going to be<b> an exploration of religion </b>(</span>
  <span id="freeText4153704078689494257" style="display:none">I knew I'd love this one!! I just needed !! to hurry up !! and read it. (Wow I am just so behind on so many releases.) This was so heartfelt and emotional, I just truly felt my soul flooded with feelings, hopeful ones and hurt ones. It's the kind of book that can brilliantly draw you in and paint you a whole world of feelings with just a few lines. The author is a master with words and these skills...I just. It's such a good book.<br /><br />I didn't realise this was going to be<b> an exploration of religion </b>(shh no i forget to read blurbs and it pains me daily) and that's honestly a topic I usually avoid. My teen years were heavily religious too and there was a lot of input into my life that I regret now. (But didn't know to regret <i>then</i>.) I loved watching Xiamora explore her feelings about religion, feel clamped into silence and shamed for not conforming how her mother demanded her to. I also liked that it didn't put a big X over religion or the church. It drew a very clear line between the mother's fanaticism (she was abusive too ngl) vs the kind priests guidance and counsel. The ending broke me, but then...it threaded through hope. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tbh I think there was too much fast forgiveness. 15 years the mother has been horrible to her daughter over religion, to the point of abuse, and Xiamora forgives her in a single afternoon. Ayyy maybe I am a cold stone. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b> I loved the relationships and friendships so so strongly</b>. Like the Xiamora's love and protection of her softest queer (super closeted too because of their parents) brother and her hard-headed but loving best friend. And also Aman! I mean, he was dubious, in the way teen boys are. But I did like him. Also Isabel was a gift and I would take a whole book about her thx. <br /><br /><b>And the writing?</b> Beautiful. Powerful. It evoked images with mere sentences and it was so easy to be caught up in the turmoil and emotion of Xiamora's thoughts. I ached with her, I wanted to cry at the ending. I want this girl to grow up and be proud of her voice, her thoughts, her decisions. I just *clenches fist* felt things.<br /><br /><b>Ok so I definitely recommend this one.</b> !!! just in case the gushing was too subtle!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4153704078689494257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2343112092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343112092" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343112092?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=contemporaries">contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=favorite-female-characters">favorite-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way">broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=poems-and-prose">poems-and-prose</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343112092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11252295668490457148"><b>4 Stars</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “And I think about all the things we could be if we were never told our bodies were not built for them.”</blockquote>
</i> <br/><br/>15-year old Xiomara lives in a world where her mother controls her life at home and society tries to limit her elsewhere. <b>But Xiomara will not be silenced.</b> She discovers the world of slam poetry and finds her voice.<br/><br/>The whole story is written in verse, and I found the audiobook particularly powerful, as <b>Xiomara uses her poetry to articulate and fight against the daily injustice in</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11252295668490457148" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b> <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “And I think about all the things we could be if we were never told our bodies were not built for them.”</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />15-year old Xiomara lives in a world where her mother controls her life at home and society tries to limit her elsewhere. <b>But Xiomara will not be silenced.</b> She discovers the world of slam poetry and finds her voice.<br /><br />The whole story is written in verse, and I found the audiobook particularly powerful, as <b>Xiomara uses her poetry to articulate and fight against the daily injustice in her life.</b> This includes her complicated relationship with her very religious and controlling mother, the rape culture prevalent at her school, and how she’s been taught to view her femininity negatively. <b>These were all important topics handled with depth and care.</b> <br /><br />Overall, I found these poems <b>incredibly intimate and raw.</b> You don’t just spend time in Xiomara’s head, but instead in the gaping wound in her chest. You feel what <i>she</i> feels. Because of this, her development felt particularly personal and I stayed completely invested. <br /><br />I do feel the resolution was slightly rushed. <b>Certain abuses were forgiven very easily</b> and it made me a little uneasy. While I liked the ending, it felt less organic than the rest of the story. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion:</b> <br /><br />This is an intense story that focuses on a complex girl and the power of voice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11252295668490457148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3545302241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3545302241" />
    <a title="JanB " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/260116-janb"><img alt="JanB " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527313486p2/260116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3545302241?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JanB " class="user" itemprop="url" name="JanB " href="/user/show/260116-janb">JanB </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/260116-janb?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/260116-janb?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/260116-janb?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3545302241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10434504313806224951">I admit I fell victim to the hype. YA and poetry is not usually my thing but I wanted to step outside my comfort zone. Given that this was so short, I thought it was worth a shot given all the 4 & 5 star reviews. <br/><br/>X, the main character, finds escape from her strict (some would say abusive) household through her poetry. I loved that a teenager can find solace and comfort in something so creative. She has a mother who is a turbo Catholic in all the worst ways. X is full of doubts and questions, as </span>
  <span id="freeText10434504313806224951" style="display:none">I admit I fell victim to the hype. YA and poetry is not usually my thing but I wanted to step outside my comfort zone. Given that this was so short, I thought it was worth a shot given all the 4 &amp; 5 star reviews. <br /><br />X, the main character, finds escape from her strict (some would say abusive) household through her poetry. I loved that a teenager can find solace and comfort in something so creative. She has a mother who is a turbo Catholic in all the worst ways. X is full of doubts and questions, as are most teens. Her awakening sexuality and a budding romance is something that sends her mother over the edge. X needs a supportive adult to help her through such a confusing time, but her father is emotionally absent and her mother is cold and harsh.<br /><br />There are some contradictory themes that bothered me, and the ending was disappointedly predictable. My issues were not with the poetry or the structure of the book but with the plot. I'm not sure who the intended audience is for this book, but it was not me. If I had a young teen I would want to read it alongside him or her to discuss it.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2217335514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6161430879985115622">wow this book COMPLETELY blew me away<br/><br/>I’m a huge fan of poetry (whether it be slam or otherwise), and I had a feeling this would be a great book. <b>I wasn’t expecting an emotion-packed, gut-wrenching, hard-hitting story like this.</b> I think this is such an IMPORTANT book today; it’s from the perspective of a Dominican fat teen, it shows just how powerful words are whether they break or heal you, and it discusses all different types of relationships and learning to climb back up when everything (or ev</span>
  <span id="freeText6161430879985115622" style="display:none">wow this book COMPLETELY blew me away<br /><br />I’m a huge fan of poetry (whether it be slam or otherwise), and I had a feeling this would be a great book. <b>I wasn’t expecting an emotion-packed, gut-wrenching, hard-hitting story like this.</b> I think this is such an IMPORTANT book today; it’s from the perspective of a Dominican fat teen, it shows just how powerful words are whether they break or heal you, and it discusses all different types of relationships and learning to climb back up when everything (or everyone) has left you broken<br /><br />and while I’m not struggling with my religion right now, and I generally don’t like religion talks in books, <b>the religion discussion here meant a lot to me</b>. I’m not limited by others because of their religious beliefs, but I’ve faced different types and levels of oppression by religious people because I’m not Christian. and even though it’s not the same, I could really really connect to what Xiomara was feeling<br /><br />maybe slightly longer review to come? <b>this is such a beautiful and impactful, please please pick it up!!!</b><br /><br /><b>:: rep ::</b> Dominican fat female MC, Dominican gay twin brother, Trinidadian male love interest, possibly-Dominican friend (?)<br /><b>:: content warnings ::</b> parental physical &amp; emotional abuse, nonconsensual sexual contact, fatphobia (challenged)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6161430879985115622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VKerkwdtr228Kkg0vO9xprpQmTtTb2kFiRS/NgWHM1Eo3I7i5VvBxeWsAZzRhiK/9RJNOoE43QOxjcYYqyDynw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

This remarkable reimagining of Dr. Ibram X. Kendi\'s National Book Award-winning Stamped from the Beginning reveals the history of racist ideas in America, and inspires hope for an antiracist future. It takes you on a race journey from then to now, shows you why we feel how we feel, and why the poison of racism lingers. It also proves that while racist ideas have always been easy to fabricate and distribute, they can also be discredited. Through a gripping, fast-paced, and energizing narrative written by beloved award-winner Jason Reynolds, this book shines a light on the many insidious forms of racist ideas--and on ways readers can identify and stamp out racist thoughts in their daily lives.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"9946568124202441397\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9976754103144882665">ELIZABETH ACEVEDO is a New York Times bestselling author of The Poet X, With the Fire on High, and Clap When You Land. Her critically-acclaimed debut novel, The Poet X, won the 2018 National Book Award for Young People’s Literature. She is also the recipient of the Printz Award for Excellence in Young Adult Fiction, the CILIP Carnegie Medal, and the Boston Globe-Hornbook Award. Additionally, she w</span>
  <span id="freeText9976754103144882665" style="display:none">ELIZABETH ACEVEDO is a New York Times bestselling author of The Poet X, With the Fire on High, and Clap When You Land. Her critically-acclaimed debut novel, The Poet X, won the 2018 National Book Award for Young People’s Literature. She is also the recipient of the Printz Award for Excellence in Young Adult Fiction, the CILIP Carnegie Medal, and the Boston Globe-Hornbook Award. Additionally, she was honored with the 2019 Pure Belpré Author Award for celebrating, affirming, and portraying Latinx culture and experience.<br /> <br />Her books include, Beastgirl &amp; Other Origin Myths (YesYes 2016), The Poet X (HarperCollins, 2018), &amp; With The Fire On High (HarperCollins, 2019), and Clap When You Land (HarperCollins, 2020).<br /><br />She holds a BA in Performing Arts from The George Washington University and an MFA in Creative Writing from the University of Maryland. Acevedo has been a fellow of Cave Canem, Cantomundo, and a participant in the Callaloo Writer’s Workshops. She is a National Poetry Slam Champion, and resides in Washington, DC with her love.</span>
